### [313] [A virtual-variable-length method for robust inverse kinematics of multi-segment continuum robots](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02256)
*Weiting Feng,Federico Renda,Yunjie Yang,Francesco Giorgio-Serchi*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: Introduces Virtual-Variable-Length (VVL) method for inverse kinematics of two-to-seven-segment continuum manipulators, adding fictitious segment-length variations to create virtual axial DOFs that improve convergence and reduce deadlocks; outperforms Jacobian-based and DLS solvers; evaluated on over 1.8 million randomized trials, achieving up to 20% higher convergence success and 40–80% fewer iterations, with boundary-proximal configurations identified as a frequent failure mode mitigated by VVL.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Conventional Jacobian-based IK solvers often suffer slow convergence or non-convergence (deadlock), especially for continuum manipulators and when initialized from neutral configurations; a robust method that mitigates initialization sensitivity and boundary effects is needed.

Method: Propose Virtual-Variable-Length (VVL) by introducing fictitious variations in segment lengths during the iteration, effectively adding virtual axial degrees of freedom to ease constraint handling and improve convergence; perform large-scale comparisons against benchmark Jacobian-based and Damped Least Squares IK solvers using randomized trials.

Result: In 1.8×10^6 randomized trials with manipulators of 2–7 segments, VVL yields up to 20% higher convergence success and 40–80% fewer average iterations to reach target accuracy (10^-4–10^-8); deadlocks are not limited to workspace boundaries and occur at boundary-proximal configurations, which VVL mitigates statistically.

Conclusion: VVL provides a robust and faster IK method for multi-segment continuum manipulators, mitigating deadlocks and improving convergence across diverse configurations; validated via extensive simulations across numerous randomized trials.

Abstract: This paper proposes a new, robust method to solve the inverse kinematics (IK) of multi-segment continuum manipulators. Conventional Jacobian-based solvers, especially when initialized from neutral/rest configurations, often exhibit slow convergence and, in certain conditions, may fail to converge (deadlock). The Virtual-Variable-Length (VVL) method proposed here introduces fictitious variations of segments' length during the solution iteration, conferring virtual axial degrees of freedom that alleviate adverse behaviors and constraints, thus enabling or accelerating convergence. Comprehensive numerical experiments were conducted to compare the VVL method against benchmark Jacobian-based and Damped Least Square IK solvers. Across more than $1.8\times 10^6$ randomized trials covering manipulators with two to seven segments, the proposed approach achieved up to a 20$\%$ increase in convergence success rate over the benchmark and a 40-80$\%$ reduction in average iteration count under equivalent accuracy thresholds ($10^{-4}-10^{-8}$). While deadlocks are not restricted to workspace boundaries and may occur at arbitrary poses, our empirical study identifies boundary-proximal configurations as a frequent cause of failed convergence and the VVL method mitigates such occurrences over a statistical sample of test cases.

### [315] [Stop Wandering: Efficient Vision-Language Navigation via Metacognitive Reasoning](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02318)
*Xueying Li,Feng Lyu,Hao Wu,Mingliu Liu,Jia-Nan Liu,Guozi Liu*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: MetaNav introduces a metacognitive VLN agent that combines a persistent 3D semantic map, history-aware planning, and reflective correction via an LLM to guide frontier selection, achieving state-of-the-art results with fewer VLM queries.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing training-free VLN agents rely on greedy frontier selection and passive memory, leading to inefficiencies such as local oscillation and redundant revisits; there is a need for metacognitive capabilities that monitor progress, diagnose failures, and adapt strategy.

Method: Proposed architecture MetaNav: spatial memory to build a persistent 3D semantic map; history-aware planning that penalizes revisits to improve efficiency; reflective correction that detects stagnation and uses an LLM to generate corrective rules to adjust frontier selection for exploration.

Result: Empirical results on GOAT-Bench, HM3D-OVON, and A-EQA show MetaNav achieves state-of-the-art performance and reduces VLM queries by 20.7%.

Conclusion: Metacognitive reasoning significantly enhances robustness and efficiency of training-free VLN agents, suggesting broader applicability of memory–planning–correction loops in embodied vision-language tasks.

Abstract: Training-free Vision-Language Navigation (VLN) agents powered by foundation models can follow instructions and explore 3D environments. However, existing approaches rely on greedy frontier selection and passive spatial memory, leading to inefficient behaviors such as local oscillation and redundant revisiting. We argue that this stems from a lack of metacognitive capabilities: the agent cannot monitor its exploration progress, diagnose strategy failures, or adapt accordingly. To address this, we propose MetaNav, a metacognitive navigation agent integrating spatial memory, history-aware planning, and reflective correction. Spatial memory builds a persistent 3D semantic map. History-aware planning penalizes revisiting to improve efficiency. Reflective correction detects stagnation and uses an LLM to generate corrective rules that guide future frontier selection. Experiments on GOAT-Bench, HM3D-OVON, and A-EQA show that MetaNav achieves state-of-the-art performance while reducing VLM queries by 20.7%, demonstrating that metacognitive reasoning significantly improves robustness and efficiency.
